14 PROJECT SUMMARY SHEETS
14.1 Introduction
In accordance with article 18, letter n), of D.S N°40/2012 Regulation of the Evaluation System of
Environmental Impact (RSEIA), and with the purpose of facilitating the inspection referred to in article 64 of the Law
N°19,300 of 1994 modified by Law 20,417 of 2010, below are the summary sheets
for the following contents of the EIA:
• Project description;
• Prediction and evaluation of the environmental impact of the project or activity;
• Detailed description of those effects, characteristics or circumstances of article 11 of
the Law.
• Plan of Measures
Mitigation, Repair and Compensation.
• Contingency and Emergency Prevention Plan
• Monitoring Plan for relevant Environmental Variables, in accordance with the provisions of
Paragraph 3 of Title VI of this Regulation.
• Compliance plan with applicable environmental legislation.
• Description of voluntary environmental commitments.
In each Sheet a column has been included that indicates the numeral of the respective chapter, including its
page, associated with the topic in question

i) Primary entry typology
The Project is framed in the following typology established in Article 10 LBGMA and Article 3
of the RSEIA:
i) Mining development projects, including coal, oil and gas, including the
prospecting, exploitation, processing plants and waste and waste disposal, as well as the
industrial extraction of aggregates, peat or clay.
Specifically, it is noted that:
i.1. Mining development projects will be understood as those actions or works whose purpose is the extraction
or benefit from one or more mining deposits and whose mineral extraction capacity is greater than
five thousand tons per month (5,000 t/month).
In its operation phase, the Project contemplates a monthly extraction greater than 5,000 tons/month, which
Main typology and will be conditioned to the characteristics of the resource to be exploited, profitability of the mineral, Chapter 1,
secondary climatic conditions, among other factors. section 1.4.4
ii) Secondary entry typology
The Project also contemplates the development of a series of complementary activities that
configure the “secondary” income typology, which are included in law 19,300 and in the RSEIA and
which are also susceptible to c
cause environmental impact, which are described below:
i.3. Waste and sterile disposal projects will be understood as those in which
massive mining waste resulting from the extraction or benefit, such as overburden, ore
low grade, mineral waste treated by leaching, tailings, slag and other equivalents, which
come from one or more mining development projects that, by themselves or as a whole, have a
extraction capacity considered in letter i.1. former.

ñ.4. Production, disposal or reuse of corrosive or reactive substances that takes place during a

Storage capacity of corrosive or reactive substances in a quantity equal to or greater than
one hundred and twenty thousand kilograms (120,000 kg).
Corrosive substances will be understood as those indicated in Class 8 of NCh 382. Of 2004, or
the one that replaces it.
Reactive substances will be understood as those indicated in Class 5 of NCh 382. Of 2004, or those
to replace it.
The waste will be considered corrosive or reactive substances if they are found in the hypotheses of the
articles 17 or 16 of Supreme Decree No. 148, of 2003, of the Ministry of Health, respectively, or that
to replace it. For the purposes of its disposal or reuse, the provisions of the letter must be followed.
or.9. of this article.
The Project will use, at an industrial level and in a sealed manner, dangerous corrosive substances during
the operation in the processing plant, among which is:
• Sulfuric acid with a consumption rate of 25,000 kg/day with storage capacity
30 m3; that is, approximately 56,000 kg,
• Sodium hydroxide with a consumption rate of 1,600 kg/day with storage capacity
80 m3; that is, approximately 90,000 kg,
The sum of the storage capacity of these 2 reagents exceeds 120,000 kg, therefore,
applies as a secondary type of income.

1
The location of the Project is justified by the presence of clays rich in Rare Earths, which in terms
extraction and processing present several environmental advantages over other types of
deposit; That is, it does not use explosives and does not require crushing or grinding processes. . During the
Justification of the last decade the mining sector has gradually opened towards sustainable exploration and extraction Chapter 1,
location of strategic minerals. Among these are the rare earths (Dysprosium, Terbium, Neodymium and section 1.8.5
Praseodymium), essential in the current economy because they are used in the manufacture, among others, of
technology and its applications in electromobility and in the generation of wind energy, keys to the
decarbonization and the use of clean energy. .

Rare Earths are directly linked to global and national efforts to mitigate the
advance of greenhouse gases and position Chile as a relevant geopolitical actor for
the decarbonization of the planet, contributing and advancing in the development and use of cleaner energy
such as electromobility and wind energy generation.
The climatic risks in the Project site area were evaluated based on the
background information available in the Climate Risk Atlas (ARClim) of the Ministry of the Environment, and
are described in greater detail in Annex 1-12 “Climate Risk Assessment”, this in line with the
“Methodological guide for the consideration of climate change in the SEIA” (SEA, 2023). According to
the information available for the commune of Penco, the Project is located in an area exposed to
a set of climate risks, as described below:
Risks related to decreased precipitation: Observations from the historical period
(1985-2019) show a significant trend of decrease in precipitation on a scale
annually (Dichato station) and in the months of April (Carriel Sur) and May (Cancha Los Litres). As for
future projections of decreased rainfall, these remain with trends
Consideration of the variable
Chapter 1,
climate change in the negative, although not all models present statistical significance for this result.
section 1.8.5.1
environmental assessment of • Risk of hydrological drought: a sharp increase in the risk of hydrological drought is projected
Annex 1-11
Project between the historical period (1980-2010) and the future period (2035-2065).
• Risk to rural domestic water security: a sharp increase in risk is projected
on rural domestic water security due to increased incidence of droughts
meteorological.
• Risk of loss of flora and fauna species due to changes in precipitation: projected
a high risk of loss of diversity of flora species and fauna species as a result of
Future change in average annual precipitation.
• Fire risk in native forests: a slight increase in fire risk is projected. The
low risk assessment is explained by the very low exposure (proportion of surface
communal area covered by native forests).
Risks related to high precipitation events: in relation to high precipitation events, the
number of days in which precipitation exceeds the P95th percentile of the record (R95%) does not present a
clear pattern of increase or decrease, except for the summer season, for which it is presented
a greater significance of increases in this type of events.

LOCATION EIA Reference
• Risk of flooding due to river overflows: there is no history of the risk of flooding.
floods due to river overflows specifically in the commune of Penco. taking as
reference relatively close communes, this risk is evaluated for the period 2035-2065 without
changes for the commune of Concepción and Talcahuano.
• Risk of flooding due to overflow of collectors: there is no history on the
risk of flooding due to river overflows specifically in the commune of Penco. taking
as a reference relatively close communes, this risk is evaluated for the period 2035-
2065 increasing for the commune of Concepción and decreasing for the commune of
Talcahuano.
Risks related to rising temperatures: The analysis of the historical period (1985-2019) gives
account of a sustained increase in temperature indicators, which occurs for the temperature
minimum in summer, number of warm nights (days in which the minimum temperature exceeds the
P90 percentile of the record) and number of summer days (days in which the maximum temperature exceeds the
25°C). Projections for the future period (2020-2054) under a climate change scenario present
significant evidence of increase in indicators such as warm days and warm nights, although in
In some cases the trend in these indicators becomes less intense in the future period than in the future.
historical period.
• Risk to the health of the population generated by heat waves: a low increase is projected
between periods. This index is expressed in terms of the change in the risk level between the
historical and future period.
• Risk of loss of flora and fauna species due to changes in the average annual temperature: the
risk of loss of flora and fauna species is assessed in the future period at a very high level.
low for flora and low for fauna.
The project is located mainly in the Commune of Penco, however, part of the surface of the
Maite and Luna extraction zones, is located in the commune of Concepción on the border with the commune of
Penco. Considering that the location of the Project is determined by the availability of the
natural resources to be extracted, it is not technically possible to evaluate alternative locations that
tend to reduce climate risks. Applicable climate risks are considered
in the Contingency and Emergency Prevention Plan. It should be noted that in Annex 1-11 of the EIA,
presents the “Analysis of project climate scenarios” developed by the Center for Global Change

14.2.3 Parts, works and actions that make up the project
Parts and works of the project/Construction Phase Reference
Name Description Character EIA
The implementation of a work facility for the development of the Project is considered, located at
interior of the polygon that delimits the platform where the Processing Plant will be built.
In this phase, the first earthworks will be carried out, such as excavations and leveling of the
Implementation of areas to be used for the respective platforms, and coordinated planning of the use of the roads Chapter 1,
the installation of existing ones, together with the enabling of temporary roads for the construction phase. Temporary numeral
Task In this activity all the necessary actions will be carried out for the correct and timely installation of 1.10.1.1
contractor at the Project site, including the prior coordination required to
authorizations and permits, in addition to the transfer of equipment and installation of its infrastructure and services
at the Project site.
To begin the construction works of the Project, a topographical layout will be carried out, consisting of
faithfully capture or transfer to the terrain the coordinates, dimensions and shapes indicated on the plans
of project. This task will be done
in accordance with the progress of construction activities of the

The extraction of the clays will be carried out in staggered banks, which will be carried out according to progress.
of the extraction work. The project corresponds to an open pit type extraction without the use of
explosives. The extraction activities will correspond to earthworks, which will be carried out
through the use of hydraulic excavators, which will extract the clays and carry out the loading
directly to trucks for transfer to the processing plant in the case of mineral, to the area
Neptuno disposition in the case of ballast and to the plant storage area in the case of escarpment.
The loading will be carried out by hydraulic excavators with a bucket of between 3.5 and 4.5 m3 or similar,
while the transportation of ore, ballast and scarp will be carried out by road-type hopper trucks.
with a maximum capacity of 20 m3 or similar. The excavator, to carry out the operation

The project processing plant considers the production of rare earth carbonate in the form
of concentrate. The raw material for the process is clay with rare earths, which is received in the
Plant and fed to the “Preparation and Classification” stage of the material for the separation of
larger material (about 1 mm). Then, it is fed to an “Earth Extraction” circuit.
Rare” from which a solution is obtained that goes to the “Precipitation of Impurities” stage and a
solution that goes to the “Solid/Liquid Separation and Washing” stage. In this stage, a
Chapter 1,
Operation Solid and liquid separation plant generating, on the one hand, washed clays that will be taken to the numeral Zone
Permanent
Disposal (ZD) processing, a solution that goes to the “Rare Earth Extraction” stage and a solution of 1.11.2.6
washing that is conducted to the “Water Recovery System”. The solution with rare and purified earths
of impurities continues towards the “Rare Earth Precipitation” area, where the rare earths are
precipitate and separate to produce a rare earth concentrate, which is packaged, stored
and later sent to marketing. The liquid phases obtained from the separation processes
solid/liquid are treated in a water recovery system to be recirculated to the process with
the purpose of generating a closed circuit to recover water and reagents, optimize the extraction of the

product from the material and reduce the necessary water supply in the processing plant,
thus leaving a reduced consumption of industrial or “make up” water, in a closed circuit and preventing the

Liquid Industrial Waste (RILES)
During the operation phase, the industrial water used in the Processing Plant will be
recirculated in a system called “closed circuit”, which will allow the reagents to be recovered
and water, thus reusing the water used, so no industrial waste will be generated
liquids of any kind coming from the production process in the Plant. The washed clays
resulting from the mixing process and countercurrent reaction with a solvent solution
(free of reagents), corresponds to a solid material that will have a moisture content of
around 20%, which will be compacted through layers at the time of disposal,
forming a physically and chemically stable fill in the Neptune Disposal Zone (ZD).
Household Solid Waste (RSD)
Household and Household Solid Waste (RSD) corresponds
mainly food waste, food packaging, beverage containers, paper, cardboard
contaminated, plastics, glass containers, among others. The withdrawal of the RSD will be carried out by a
third party authorized by the SEREMI de Salud, with a frequency of 3 times per week. will be verified
that the transportation and final disposal of waste comply with all health authorizations
for their transportation and final destination. More information Annex 10-6 PASM 140 of the EIA.
Non-Hazardous Industrial Waste (RISES)
They correspond to iron cuttings, packaging materials, wood cuttings, remains of
HDPE, existing pipes (due to construction of the pipeline modification), among others. The retirement
of this type of waste will be carried out by an authorized third party with a frequency of 2 times per

Characteristic effect or significant adverse effects on the quantity and quality of renewable natural resources,

circumstance: including soil, water and air
Carbon sink:
The project will be located in a matrix of forest plantations, which do not comply with the
characteristics necessary to be considered sinks of natural origin. Although in certain
stages of development in which the plantations are in active growth have a
net carbon capture, when evaluating its complete life cycle, carbon is stored
temporarily in the biomass of the plantations, but this capture is released again to the
atmosphere as a consequence of forest harvesting or within the useful life of the products
forests, this situation being able to be used analogously for the felling of plantations that
establishes the project, whose cut surface will be returned through reforestation with
native species in a place to be defined (PAS 149). In this sense, considering its life cycle
complete, forest plantations do not capture more carbon than they emit, so they are not
considered as sinks of natural origin. Due to the above, a loss of
ecosystem climate resilience due to this concept.
Air:
Based on the analysis of literal a) and c) of article 5, it is possible to establish that the emissions
atmospheric conditions associated with the Project do not lead to significant effects in relation to
the baseline condition of the Air component (Chapter 4).

of contours that converge towards a point for monitoring. For its part, groundwater

and in the area in general, because it corresponds to a sector with substrate with little capacity
infiltration and hydrogeological importance.
Based on the above background, it is possible to conclude that the Project will generate effects
significant adverse effects on the quantity and quality of renewable natural resources, due to
the loss is ground (literal a and c).

Archaeological Cultural Heritage
The archaeological survey carried out on the occasion of the EIA (Chapter 3 “Base Line” Section C
Cultural Heritage), recognized only one archaeological site, called PMP-SA-01,
corresponding to an isolated discovery of ceramic fragments of smoothed surfaces (interior and

14.5 Risks to the health of the population
In accordance with the analysis presented in Chapter 5 on the effects, characteristics or circumstances of article 11 of Law 19,300, the Project enters
as an Environmental Impact Study due to risk to the health of the population, referred to in letter a) of article 11 of the Law. Note that, not
will generate liquid effluents, waste or noise emissions for which there is no quality or emission standard in Chile or in the states of
reference indicated in article 11 of the RSEIA. Given the above, a specific chapter is required regarding potential health risks.
of the population, which is presented in Annex 5-1.

In accordance with the name of the measure, the implementation method consists of three (3) phases or activities:
germplasm collection, nursery and planting, which are described below.
Germplasm collection:
The generation of individuals is contemplated from the local collection of seeds, in addition to obtaining material
vegetative from non-lignified branches (cuttings) of individuals phenotypically selected for eventual
rooting, coming from the local population, that is, from the area of influence of flora and vegetation of the Project
and its surroundings.
Depending on the type of propagule in question (part of the plant capable of developing separately to
give rise to a new organism identical to the one that formed it), the collection will be carried out at the appropriate station according to
the phenology of the species, to present its occurrence and adequate quality for collection.
- Fruits/Seeds: The collection will be carried out in the period between the months of February and May.

- Stakes: Stakes will be collected
about 20 cm long, from corresponding new shoots
to the growth of the period. Different collection campaigns will be carried out, starting in mid-
spring to late summer.
The accessions will be carried out by trained personnel, who will use cutting tools in good condition,
mainly pruning shears and/or chime, which will be properly cleaned and disinfected
with alcohol prior to taking each sample, trying to make clean cuts in order not to cause damage to the
mother tree.
A record sheet will be prepared for each sample, where the following information will be collected:
- Sample type
- Date of sample collection
- Location point, in UTM WGS 84 18S coordinates
- Collector name
- State of development of the individual
- Health status
- Vigor
- Photographic record
A database will be created of the sampling campaigns carried out and each sample will be
duly labeled with an identifier that allows for traceability of it, for the activities
later associated with the measure.
The total amount of propagules to be collected must be at least triple the commitment in the case of seeds and
quintuple in the case of cuttings and the necessary corms. The objective is that at the time of planting there is
with adequate production that allows us to meet the 2,990 ECC copies, maintaining the remaining
as a safeguard to carry out the plantation.
Nursery:
For this stage, an appropriate infrastructure will be created to allow the treatment required to be carried out.
propagate the collected material or an agreement will be established with a nursery in the area that can carry out the
14-88
==================================================================================
PAGE 93
==================================================================================
Chapter 14
Summary Tabs
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
MC-04: Germplasm Collection, Nursery and Replanting of Individuals of Asplenium trilobum, Gardoquia multiflora and Vestia foetida EIA Reference
work in accordance with the methodology detailed below. This infrastructure will be in operation
prior to starting the germplasm collection campaigns.
At this stage, it is proposed to study methodologies to increase the germination of material from fruits.
collected, with different stratification and scarification treatments. The fruits will be characterized in terms of
size, maturity and origin in order to evaluate the effect of any of these variables on germination in
nursery conditions. In the nursery, different substrates and containers will be tested in order to select the
combination most suitable for obtaining plants that can be planted in the field. They will characterize the
plant quality indices (slenderness index, stem-root index and Dickson index).
In general, it is expected that the plants, arranged in planting bags, will be kept in the nursery for
two (2) years, a period after which it will be decided if they are in a position to be taken to the areas of
plantation. This decision will be determined by the observed growth and vigor of the individuals produced in
nursery. If it is considered insufficient, individuals will require an additional year (1) of maintenance.
Planting:
Planting should ideally be done in late autumn or early winter. To carry out this activity
The following general measures will be considered.
Throughout the area of execution of the measure, access will be blocked to prevent the entry of herbivores such as
horses, goats, cattle and sheep; and people outside the Project, with the aim of improving the conditions of the
establishment and survival of specimens. The measure must allow or facilitate the transit of local fauna.
As far as possible, rubbing against the native vegetation present will be avoided, prioritizing the establishment of the
plants under the protection of bushes, so that a nurse effect is generated. The preparation of this anodizing
It will be carried out individually so as to affect the surrounding vegetation as little as possible. The plantation
will be based on the existence of microsites suitable for the development of the species of interest.
A preparation of the land will be done with the ob
aimed at decompacting and increasing infiltration capacity,
through individual preparation of the boxes. It will be carried out by manual drilling of one dimension
approximately 50x50x50 cm, with an improvement of the substrate, which includes the addition of soil from sectors in the
that the species are currently found. The above, with the aim of eventually providing natural inoculums
14-89

MC-04: Germplasm Collection, Nursery and Replanting of Individuals of Asplenium trilobum, Gardoquia multiflora and Vestia foetida EIA Reference
that contribute to the best establishment of the specimens. In them the substrate will be decompressed and a
mixture composed, preferably, of 10% of plant material and 90% of the substrate of the box.
One day before planting, the empty boxes will be flooded with water to promote infiltration and
soil decompaction. Then the plant will be placed inside the box, remaining below the level of the surface.
of the soil and subsequent work will be carried out to form a cup around the plant. The excess substrate is
will spread around the box.
At the time of planting, an establishment irrigation consisting of 5 liters per plant will be applied. The frequency
Irrigation will be biweekly in autumn and spring, and weekly in summer. An amount between 5 to 8 lt/plant will be applied.
each time, for the first two (2) years. After the first two (2) years of irrigation of the plantation have elapsed,
An attempt will be made to acclimatize the individuals to the local environmental conditions, from the third year to the fifth.
For this, a decreasing irrigation program in volume and frequency is considered during the two (2) years.
later, watering at the end of the process (fifth year) only in case of risks of mortality and state of the plants
and finally eliminating it completely. This program will be subject to the evaluation and monitoring of the situation
climate prevailing in the plantation areas.
In order to avoid attack by lagomorphs and damage by herbivory, additional protections will be provided.
individual around each plant, which will be mesh or, failing that, polypropylene with Anti-
UV, attached to a stake using wires, 0.6 m high. In a complementary manner, and if necessary,
will implement a lagomorph control plan, which will exclude chemical control.
Maintenance of the plantation will be carried out during the five (5) years after its execution, where the
individual protections and the irrigation system, if any problem or deterioration is registered, the repair will proceed.
In addition, there will be control by manual elimination and subsequent management of the presence of invasive species such as
such as: Acacia dealbata, Acacia saligna, Pinus radiata, Rubus ulmifolius and Rosa rubiginosa, to avoid competition
with natural vegetation and favor the regeneration niches of native components.
If mortality of individuals is observed during the two (2) years after planting, they must
be replanted during the following autumn/winter/spring season, in order to maintain the number of ECC
initial corresponding to 2,990 copies in the enrichment sector.

The objective of the measure is to carry out a rescue and relocation activity, in order to avoid the loss of
Section 7.3.3
Target individuals of fauna with low mobility due to the Project. Added to the species mentioned above, it will apply

Capture activities will be carried out by specialist professionals with accredited experience in
manipulation of wild fauna, and will be carried out once the capture permit granted by the
authority and made the respective notification.
Description
• Amphibians: will be carried out through manual capture through active tours and/or directed search of the
target species, in the habitats and environments in which it is present in the area of influence of the Project.

• Reptiles: it will be carried out by manual capture and/or with a sliding snare through active routes and/or
directed search for the target species, in the habitats and environments in which it is present in the area of
influence of the Project.
• Micromammals: the capture will be carried out with collapsible Sherman and/or Tomahawk-type traps modified,
by installing them in grids or lines, in the habitats and environments of this group that are present in
the area of influence of the Project. The traps will be baited (oats and banana) and checked twice by
day, to be active for a period of approx. 8 to 12 hours maximum. Three repetitions will be carried out
for each grid or capture line, this means that the traps will be installed for three nights
consecutive before starting the rescue on a new grid, as mentioned in the Technical Guide for
Implement Rescue/Relocation and Controlled Disturbance Measures (Torres-Mura et al., 20142) of the
Agricultural Service and Livestock
dero. In the case of D. gliroides, the modified Tomahawk traps will be
installed at height, using banana as bait.
The measure is justified by its ability to reduce the loss of individuals belonging to the target species and
Justification
those with low mobility (PASM 146).

hectares, which include works and parts of the Project (areal works), both temporary and
permanent.

implementation opportunity). The activities will be carried out prior to the intervention and/or the advancement of the
construction and construction machinery, with captures being made in a maximum of five days (between
1 to 5 days) before the start of the different work fronts. For this, capture permits will be requested.
corresponding to the Agricultural and Livestock Service (SAG), previously informing the work days according to the
frequency stipulated in the resolution issued by the authority.
Capture
Approximately two months before the start of capture activities, for each rescue area,
a baseline campaign in order to corroborate and adjust the estimate of the number of individuals to rescue,
considering the natural variation that the density of this species may suffer in relation to the availability of
food, shelter and/or bodies or water courses.
The capture effort will be carried out between 8:00 p.m. and 2:00 a.m. to coincide with the increase in activity that
amphibians present during twilight hours. In the case of reptiles, the work will be carried out during the day.
between 9:00 a.m. and 5:00 p.m., the time when individuals are most active. On the other hand, for the
small mammals, the work will concentrate on the installation of traps during daylight hours (maximum time
without
review during the 8-hour day) and subsequent review every night between 08:00 and 11:00 am.
The area to be intervened will be covered on foot, trying to carry out a complete sweep, with particular attention to
emphasis on those microenvironments favorable for the presence of the target species, such as bushes and
rockeries for small mammals, bodies or watercourses for amphibians and rockeries, bushes and trees in the case
of reptiles. For the capture, the exploration of the different environments and microenvironments will be carried out by carrying out the
active search for specimens under or between stones, logs and bushes. Detected individuals will be captured
manually (herpetofauna) or Sherman traps (micromammals).
Transportation
The captured specimens will be placed individually in plastic containers, which will be provided with
adequate substrate and shelter, along with the humidity, ventilation and temperature conditions necessary to
ensure the well-being of the specimens.
Each individual will remain in its container for no more than three hours.
14-96
==================================================================================
PAGE 101
==================================================================================
Chapter 14
Summary Tabs
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
MM-02 Rescue and Relocation Plan EIA Reference
Individuals will be transported on the outside of the van, avoiding drafts or direct sunlight; and
trying to maintain biosafety measures due to the risk of zoonoses.
Marking and release
Prior to their release, the captured specimens will be characterized in terms of their state of health.
development, sex, and basic morphometric parameters.
The amphibians will not receive any type of mark and will be individualized through photographs and registration on identification cards.
characteristics for later recognition (sex, warts, coloration, etc.).
For the release of the specimens, areas will be selected that correspond to the same types of environment in which
the capture was made. To choose the release area, an evaluation of the quality of the environments will be carried out.
and microenvironments, considering factors such as: presence of the species, degree of protection of the area, availability
of food resources and shelters, among others.
Monitoring
After the measure is applied, a first monitoring will be carried out in the capture area the next day or 2 days
After the rescue (immediate monitoring) focused on verifying that there are no individuals left to rescue, this will last
four days and eventually more if necessary. The activities associated with the construction process may
start once the first monitoring of the capture area is completed within a maximum period of 5 days.
The following monitoring, corresponding to the second campaign, will be carried out 14 days after the rescue in the
relocation area, focused on determining the early permanence of the relocated individuals, since the
Paint marking should withstand this period of time. The third, fourth and fifth monitoring will be carried out at the
90, 180 and 360 days after the rescue, the objective of said monitoring being to be able to evaluate the behavior of
the receiving population once new individuals are added. The duration of the monitoring will last
three days. The monitoring covers a full year to include a reproductive cycle of the target species.

• Once the disturbance itself has been applied, routes and/or sampling points will be made, with the

If the deadline is exceeded, the measure must be repeated due to the possible recolonization of the target species of the

Description habitat of origin.
The habitat of origin of the species corresponds to environments mostly with some degree of intervention, associated
to existing roads, vehicular traffic areas, exotic or forest type vegetation
such. The target species
corresponds to species with the capacity to adapt to these intervened environments, and can be found on shores
road, stones or small shelters close to existing works, in environments mainly of type
forest plantation or scrub.
Potential target habitat.
The destination areas of the animals correspond to areas similar to those of origin due to their proximity.
In particular, it is mainly constituted by areas intervened by existing roads, forest plantations and
bushes located on the edges of intervened areas. In the destination areas and according to information collected in
field campaigns, the presence of target species was evident, providing adequate conditions for
receive disturbed individuals.
Degree of influence of other activities on the site where the animals are planned to be moved
As already mentioned, the destination area of the animals corresponds to areas with medium to high intervention, despite
To this end, the habitat represents adequate conditions to receive the animals. It should be noted that the owner must
provide protection of these areas, safeguarding them from future interventions.

Home range and movement capacity of target species
According to scientific literature, the home range of the reptiles targeted by the measure would not exceed 150 m in diameter.
displacement. On the other hand, and for small mammals, the displacement would not exceed 450 m. Of this
In this way, the measure is based on the biology and behavior of the species and their ability to escape through their
own media. Due to the above and to avoid the recolonization of animals, all types of shelter must be removed.
of animals (stones, branches, rocks, etc.) and the reception area must be environmentally enriched with everything
the removed material. Regarding movement, it is expected that the animals leave the disturbed area from
the moment the activities begin, which is why prior review is necessary, immediately after
disturbance and monitoring specified, in terms of estimating abundance and species richness.
Expected progress rate of the displacement.
As already mentioned in the previous statement, the rate of progress of animals is considered linked to their areas of activity.
home, with the target species being able to move by their own means a distance of between 150 and 450 m. By
the above, the rate of progress of the measurement will be conditioned by disturbing sequentially from the most
remote from the destination areas, conditioning the advance of the species from intervened areas to areas of
protection. It is considered that the measure should be carried out by a team made up of a wildlife specialist.
wild and 6 days' work (with tools for manual clearing, such as a chainsaw or weeder). It is considered
that the equipment already detailed will have a progress rate of 1 hectare per day of work for each crew of
workers (1 specialist and 6 daily wages).
The measure is justified, given the presence of species of reptiles and micromammals (endemic and/or in categories of
conservation according to current national legislation), which due to their low displacement capacity
Justification they present a risk of suffering loss of individuals. The application of this measure is justified on limited surfaces, in
which are suggested to facilitate the natural movement of individuals towards adjacent areas (Torres-Mura et al., 2014),
and avoid unnecessary capture stress.
This measure will apply to associated linear works, existing or new roads, modification of the
Location of the ENAP pipeline measurement and LTE intervention area mainly, which require some degree of intervention
such as vegetation clearance, steepening, compaction or other.

opportunity to • Clearing should be done primarily manually or with hand tools (chainsaw or

disturbance in the areas of origin once the activities have concluded (next day).

MC-05 Protection of areas surrounding the project EIA Reference
Measurement type Compensation

protection
Environmental impact
IFA-02. Loss and/or modification of habitat of species of interest and/or sensitive - Amphibians, Reptiles and Mammals

Project Phase Construction and Operation
The objective of the measure is to ensure the existence of patches of native and exotic vegetation, which as a whole and with
a determined spatial distribution, allow the persistence of populations of the target species.
Objective The measure focuses mainly on the species: Pudu puda (pudú), Leopardus guigna (güiña) and Puma concolor
(cougar). However, it is considered that the measure will benefit a larger group of species by allowing the
habitat permanence for them.
Chapter 7,
The measure consists of the protection of a series of polygons surrounding and within the area of influence of the Project. Section 7.3.2
This protection translates into ensuring the permanence of its vegetation with a prohibition on clear, short or Table 7-25
any other extraction process, permanently from the beginning of the Project.
Considering the baseline of flora and vegetation, added to the photointerpretation of surrounding sectors, it has been
determined a set of polygons to be subject to this protection. These areas include sectors with
native vegetation and forest plantations.
The polygons that will be protected total 90.66 hectares, and are presented in digital format (.kmz) in the Annex
Description 7.1-3, classified according to their vegetation cover as follows:
• Native preservation forest: 4.90 hectares
• Forest plantation: 76.92 hectares
• Grassland: 4.21 hectares
• Thicket: 2.95 hectares
• Tree scrub: 1.68 hectares

==================================================================================
PAGE 112
==================================================================================
Chapter 14
Summary Tabs
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
MC-05 Protection of areas surrounding the project EIA Reference
It will be the responsibility of the Project to ensure compliance with this protection throughout the entire area.
The measure is based on the fact that those forest plantations that have certain characteristics – such as
presence of undergrowth – which are capable of becoming habitat for species of vertebrate fauna, with emphasis
in native mammals such as Pudu puda, Leopardus guigna, among others (Simonetti et al 2013). This proposal continues
the idea of designing policies that promote biodiversity-friendly practices on productive lands (Fisher et
al 2008)4, in line with the Aichi Targets indicated by the Convention on Biological Diversity in 2010.
The use that various groups of terrestrial vertebrates make of forest plantations has been widely
documented (Simonetti et al 2013, Estades et al 2012, Acosta-Jamett and Simonetti 2004, Estades 1999)5, and their
Persistence in this habitat would depend, among other factors, on the composition at the landscape scale, for example, the
distance between habitat patches, the existence of biological corridors and the absence of elements that limit the
Justification
connectivity (e.g. Acuña and Estade
s, 2011)6.
In this way, based on the vast literature available on this topic, there is recently an understanding of
the existence of certain key characteristics for the existence of a good quality habitat – at the scale of
landscape – for forest species. These characteristics are summarized according to Arroyo-Rodríguez et al (2020)7, a
broad strokes, in the maintenance of ≥ 40% forest cover, organized in at least 10% in a large
patch and the remaining 30% in various dispersed patches and corridors, also being surrounded by a matrix
anthropogenic friendly to biodiversity.
It is this theoretical-practical framework that gives justification to this measure, which seeks to approximate these standards.
to design a landscape that allows the persistence of the target species in the area.

encourage land sparing or wildlife-friendly farming. Front Ecol Environ 6(7):380-385

challenges and opportunities. University Publishing, Santiago; 2012. pp. 77–98.
Acosta-Jamett and Simonetti 2004, Habitat use by Oncifelis guigna and Pseudalopex culpaeus in a fragmented forest landscape in central Chile. Biodiversity and Conservation 13:1135-

of influence, which correspond mainly to native forest streams, patches of plantations
forests, water courses or flood zones present in the area.

• Prohibition of use of fire
• Prohibition of feeding domestic and wild species
• Prohibition of throwing waste outside established places
• Prohibition of the circulation of vehicles and workers outside authorized and established roads.

• Prohibitions and restrictions aimed at minimizing disturbances to wild species during the period.
reproductive.

The objective of the measure is to carry out a rescue and relocation activity, in order to avoid the loss of
Objective
individuals of invertebrate fauna due to the Project.
The captures will be carried out by teams with experience in the management of invertebrate fauna, each one being
led by a professional specialist in the subject. The activities will be carried out after obtaining the permit
capture granted by the competent authority (Exempt Resolution) and in accordance with the established requirements
for this one.
However, capture activities will be planned according to the rate of progress of the works, with the objective
of what
There is a maximum of 5 days between the end of the rescue and the beginning of the construction phase, to avoid
recolonization of the area. Therefore, the number of specialists and effort will depend on the surface of the works to be carried out.
release.
To carry out the captures, the field personnel (wildlife specialists) must have experience and/or
be trained in the management of target species, including the management of basic biosecurity concepts and
Description
of the contingency plan in case injured, dying or dead animals are observed.
Capture activities should be carried out during times when temperatures allow favorable conditions.
for the relocation of individuals. This is during the spring and/or summer season, and on the days and times when
The climatic characteristics allow it, adjusting the construction start schedule to what is indicated.
Specifically for captures carried out on arachnids, these must be carried out after the summer season.
(March-April) so as not to interfere with the ecdysis process or the oothecae hatching period. It should be considered
time differences for females and males; during the day for females and during the night for males.
To record the above, daily records associated with the application of the captures will be implemented, indicating
the area, professionals in charge, date, temperature and wind and cloud conditions, applied efforts and/or rate of
progress, and as well as the capture and relocation schedule of the individuals.
The measure is justified by its ability to reduce the loss of individuals belonging to the target species (PASM 146 for
Justification
invertebrate fauna).

• The relocation area will not be intervened by the Project, guaranteeing its protection in the medium to long term.

Capture activities should be carried out during times when temperatures allow favorable conditions.
for the relocation of individuals. This is during the spring and/or summer season, and on the days and times when
The climatic characteristics allow it, adjusting the construction start schedule to what is indicated.
Specifically for captures carried out on arachnids, these must be carried out after the summer season.

Below are the considerations associated with the capture of invertebrate fauna:
The characterization of invertebrates will be carried out using two main methods, an active collection and a
passive, distributed in each of the prospected sites. In each PME the surface will be covered on foot with
aid of an odometer and an active collection will be carried out under different rocks and pieces of logs available in the area of the
project, in the case of the bushes and trees that are prospected, an entomological umbrella will be used, whose function
It mainly consists of the tapping of available branches and woody structures, generating the subsequent fall and collection.
with entomological aspirator of the different species that can be observed in the white cloth blanket that makes up
the entomological umbrella used, whose surface area was one square meter. Traps will be used for passive collection.
Barber and pitfall, where it was installed following the recommendations to avoid typical errors that can affect the
data obtained with the auto-correlation between the samples according to Lafranco et al (2010). For this, pitfall traps
(Pitfall and barber trap) will be placed every 40 meters along the transect, pitfall or pitfall traps will be
made up of a 360 ml plastic cup buried at the surface and the Barber traps were also
arranged like pitfall traps, where one third of their capacity will be filled with aromatic liquid bait based on
apple cider vinegar and red grapes which will be installed randomly in each PME.

They will be transported in containers. For transport by vehicle, it will be ensured that the containers are fixed and

The arachnid group must be marked to achieve correct tracking. For the above, a marker will be required.
non-toxic fluorescent. The handling and marking procedure must be detailed in the capture permit,

for its correct function in subsequent monitoring.
Monitoring
Once the capture permit is obtained, and to comply with the Exempt Resolution that allows it, in a manner
prior to the start of the activity
ad, notice of the start of the captures will be given to the regional SAG, with 5 or 10 business days of
in advance or as stipulated in the permission granted by the Exempt Resolution.
After the measure is applied, a first monitoring will be carried out in the capture area the next day or 2 days later.
to the rescue (immediate monitoring) focused on verifying that there are no individuals left to rescue, this will last four days
and eventually more if necessary. The activities associated with the construction process may begin once
completed the first monitoring of the capture area within a maximum period of 5 days.
The following monitoring, corresponding to the second campaign, will be carried out 14 days after the rescue in the area
of relocation, focused on determining the early permanence of relocated individuals, since marking with
Paint should withstand this period of time. The third, fourth and fifth monitoring will be carried out at 90, 180 and 360
days after the rescue, the objective of said monitoring being to be able to evaluate the behavior of the population
recipient once new individuals are added. The duration of the monitoring will last three days. The
Monitoring covers a full year to include a reproductive cycle of the target species.
Notice will be given to the Superintendency of the Environment prior to carrying out each rescue activity and
Relocation indicator, and a report will be delivered after carrying out each activity. It is understood for each activity
rescue and relocation compliance that will be carried out in accordance with the construction and operation phase schedule, according to which
The rescue areas are related to the following Project works and years within each phase.

to carry out herb collection tasks.

The risk of fire in the Project is mainly associated with poor management.
inadequate handling of flammable and combustible materials, as well as work with
tools that could project incandescent particles, indicating the
following measures to minimize said risk:
• Identification of areas where any
activity that may generate sparks, such as lighting a fire, smoking,
carry or maintain elements that may cause sparks, etc.
• Implement a hot work permit system, in which
can evaluate control measures on a case-by-case basis, when they are executed
activities with open flames or incandescent particles.
• Combustible and flammable materials will be stored in spaces
specially enabled, complying with
the provisions of the D.S. No.
160/2008 of the Ministry of Economy, Development and Reconstruction “Approves
Safety Regulations for the facilities and operations of
Actions or measures to implement
production and refining, transportation, storage, distribution and
supply of liquid fuels” and in the D.S. No. 43/2016 of
Ministry of Health “Approves Regulations for the storage of
dangerous substances.”
• Arrangement of fire extinguishing elements in the facilities
appropriate (fire extinguishers, etc.), carrying out periodic maintenance, according to
is established in current regulations.
• Location of extinguishing equipment near the points
probable fire hazards, being accessible by workers and
demarcating the area where they are located according to the regulations
current.
• Training workers in the correct use of the elements of
protection and fire fighting.
• Control of combustible products, maintaining order and cleanliness in
storage and having only the necessary stock.

Action plan against earthquakes and tsunamis Reference EIA
Phase of the project to which construction, operation and closure applies.
All Project facilities, mainly in:
Part, work or associated action - Installation of tasks.

In the event that an earthquake of intensity IV or greater on the Mercalli scale occurs, the following measures will be carried out.
following actions:
• The staff will suspend any activity they are carrying out and will go to the safety zone area.
closest security, which should be located in an open area and away from
installations that may involve risk of collapse/collapse. Chapter 8,
• You should not act impulsively as this increases the risk of injury and contributes to numeral 8.7.4.3
Actions or measures to increase panic.
implement • It will be necessary to move away from the windows, since the vibration can cause the glass to break.
• If you are indoors, protect yourself from falling lamps, electrical appliances, etc.
wood, books, paintings, etc.
• It will remain in the safety zone until the earthquake ends. Only in specific cases such as
visible and considerable damage to the building such as falling walls, fractured columns
an area can be evacuated.
• In external areas of buildings, it will be necessary to move away from walls, poles, electrical cables and other
items that can fall.

Action plan against earthquakes and tsunamis Reference
EIA
• If you are handling a motorized unit, guide the unit with caution to a place
safe and the unit will be stopped.
After an earthquake:
• You must remain silent and calm.
• Depending on the magnitude of the earthquake, buildings must be completely evacuated towards
assigned security zones.
• Evacuate quickly, but without running, maintaining calm, order and silence, avoiding producing
crowds.
• If you get trapped, try to use a visible or audible signal.
• Check if there are any fire sources; report them immediately.
• Observe if there are injured people, not moving the injured unless they are in danger.
of suffering new wounds.
• Wait 30 minutes in the security zone for possible aftershocks.
• An inspection will be carried out at the facilities in order to verify their condition and rule out
existence of damage that could cause the collapse or collapse of structures.
• A damage report will be prepared and communication will be maintained with local authorities and
of emergencies.
• Work will not be activated until it has been proven that there is no risk of collapse.
structural of the facilities.

notify the immediate Supervisor, who in turn informs the Head of the Emergency to assess the situation
and coordinate the corresponding actions. As long as the emergency situation allows it, the
Trained staff members (in principle, Intervention Team) should provide the first
relevant aid.
However, if you witness an accident, the following actions should be taken into consideration:
• Do not get upset, do not scream, or run desperately for help or to help the injured person. Chapter 8,
You must remain calm and report the situation to your supervision and/or emergency numbers, section 8.7.4.5
Actions or measures to
as previously indicated.
implement
• Approach the injured person and confirm if he or she is alive, conscious, and the severity of the injuries.
their injuries. If he is conscious, you should talk to the injured person, try to calm him down and avoid
let it move.
• If the injured party is trapped, a rescue should not be attempted unless it is
extreme necessity (if a structure is giving way, if there is current, fire or water, if there is
toxic risk, etc.).
• Only if you have knowledge of first aid and the conditions of the person or those affected make it possible.
allow, you should try to provide support. The affected person should not be moved as it should always be
presume damage to the back or internal organs.

with some force to try to prevent bleeding.

health.

Action plan in case of sewage spill EIA reference
Project phase to which it applies All phases
Associated part, work or action Wastewater treatment plants and chemical baths
1. The intervention team and Emergency Chief will be notified immediately, indicating:
• Location of the incident.
• Magnitude
• Type of waste
• Consequences (severity)
2. The Emergency Chief will evaluate the situation and if warranted, will request the evacuation of personnel.
3. To stop the generation of sewage, the area must be evacuated, therefore, the boss or supervisor
in charge of this, will suspend the work in its offices, proceeding to transfer the workers
Chapter 8,
to his residence. At the same time, the external company will be called to identify, fix or replace
section 7.4.13
Actions or measures to the parts of the system that are in poor condition.
imple
ment 4. In the event that the contingency persists for a period greater than one day of operation at maximum
capacity, the water will be removed by a company with health authorization, which will take it to a site
of final disposal equally authorized.
5. A team will proceed to clean and/or disinfect the areas that have been in contact with the water.
served. In case of contact with the ground, the contaminated material will be removed and disposed of in
an authorized site.
6. Once the problem has been solved, it will be the responsibility of the boss or supervisor in charge
authorize its normal operation again.
7. An investigation of the incident will be carried out, collecting all possible evidence, in order to
make the corrections that the case warrants and avoid a new occurrence.

yield and growth obtained, the decision will be made to replant individuals,
which must be established in the report.
• Report No. 3 and No. 4: Will report, if applicable, the third year of nursery maintenance. Furthermore,
It will give a detailed account of the activities carried out prior to planting.
• Report No. 5 and No. 6: Will report on the planting of individuals and the maintenance carried out in the
period.
• Report No. 7 and No. 8: Will report on the activities carried out in the second year of maintenance and
the survival of individuals.
• Report No. 9 and No. 10: Will report on the activities carried out in the third year of maintenance and the
survival of individuals.
• Report No. 11 and No. 12: Will report on the activities carried out in the fourth year of maintenance and
the survival of individuals.
• Report N°13 and 14: Will report on the activities carried out in the fifth year of maintenance and the
survival of individuals.

▪ Presence/absence of target species
The first monitoring focuses on determining if there are individuals left in the intervention area, targeting the
0% abundance of the target species. This monitoring will take place one or two days after the rescue. The
parameter that will be used in the presence/absence of the target species, aiming at the rescue of 100% of
individuals. This monitoring and parameters to be measured will be carried out only in the capture area.
▪ Percentage of relocated individuals resighted
The second monitoring will be carried out in the relocation area and is focused on determining the
early permanence of rescued individuals in the relocation area, through identification
of marked individuals. The parameter that will be used corresponds to the resighting percentage of
relocated individuals. The second monitoring will be carried out 14 days after the rescue only in the area
of relocation.
▪ Behavior of the receiving population
- The third, fourth and fifth monitoring will be carried out in the relocation area and is focused on
determine how the receiving population behaves once new individuals are inserted.
The parameters to be evaluated will be the richness, average density and relative abundance of species.
present. The third, fourth and fifth monitoring will be carried out at 90, 180 and 360 days after the
rescue, respectively.
The permitted limits are the following:
● 0% abundance of the target species is allowed in the capture area, that is, if during the
First monitoring, more individuals of the target species are identified and these will be rescued.
Allowed limits or
● In the relocation area, the early permanence of relocated individuals in
committed
10%.
In the relocation area, the aim will be to maintain and/or increase the average density (abundance
absolute) of the target species.

To carry out the captures, the field personnel (wildlife specialists) must have
experience and/or be trained in the management of the target species.
Capture activities should be carried out during times when temperatures allow conditions
favorable for the relocation of individuals. This is during the spring and/or summer season, and in
the days and times in which the climatic characteristics allow it, adjusting the start schedule
from construction to what is indicated.
Specifically for captures carried out on arachnids, these must be carried out after the
summer season (March-April) so as not to interfere with their ecdysis process or their period of
Method or procedure of
oothecal hatching. Time differences should be considered for females and males; during the day to
measurement of each parameter
females and during the night for males.
To record the above, daily records associated with the application of the catches will be implemented,
indicating the area, professionals in charge, date, temperature and wind and cloud conditions,
efforts applied and/or rate of progress, and thus time of capture and relocation of individuals.
Below are the considerations associated with the capture of invertebrate fauna:

passive collection, distributed in each of the prospected sites. In each PME the surface will be covered
pedestrian way with the help of an odometer and an active collection will be carried out under different rocks and pieces of

exhausted from the processing plant. The floor will be redisposed on this material.

I feel:
Monitoring of the measure will be carried out from the moment the reuse of the land begins in areas
intervened already closed, for a period of 5 years.
Duration and frequency of the plan
monitoring Sampling frequency:
The monitoring will be done for the first time, after the land redisposition is carried out on
each ZE and ZD, which occurs only once in each area. Subsequently, a biannual monitoring will be carried out,

the workers.

In terms of uniqueness of the vascular flora, 19 species were registered under conservation category. Of
Of the total number of species recorded, five are threatened, corresponding to Gomortega keule,
Pitavia punctata and Vestia foetida in the Endangered category and Asplenium trilobum and Citronella mucronata in
Vulnerable category. The remaining 14 taxa correspond to species not considered threatened (Almost
Threatened and Least Concern). Although individuals of the species were recorded in the area of influence
Gomortega keule (queule) and Pitavia punctata (pitao), these will not be intervened by the project works.
With regard to vegetation, few types of vegetation structures were differentiated that, based on
In relation to its distribution and density, they allow the area under study to be segregated into cartographic units. The largest extension in
Project surface (ha) of the units corresponds to forest plantations, with the rest defined between
native bushes and forests. The importance of vegetation in terms of uniqueness is due
mainly to the presence of native forests that have within their composition the presence of
Gomortega keule, an entity in the “Endangered” conservation category, a condition that determines the high
ecosystemic importance and the great structural and functional sensitivity that these forests present to
eventual changes in the environment in which it is established. Without prejudice to what is indicated, it is worth clarifying that the areas
of native forest with the presence of Queule, as well as any unit of native forest, will not be intervened by
the Project, that is, the authorization of works and parts of the Project in the vegetation formation is not contemplated
of native forest with the presence of this species, nor in native forest units.
For all species of vascular flora that will be affected as a result of the site of the works and
parts of the Project, environmental measures related to the protection of individuals must be considered,

Regarding loading and unloading and identification of security measures, the cargo will be stowed in a manner
convenient in the vehicle and be secured by appropriate means, in order to avoid displacement
of them, among themselves and in relation to the walls and platform of the vehicle (article 8); the vehicle's engine will be
stopped while loading and unloading operations are carried out, unless its use is necessary, under
strict safety conditions, for the operation of pumps and other mechanisms that allow loading
or unloading of the vehicle, and it must be immobilized by a device that secures it, such as
wedges or other elements that prevent its movement (article 16).
Vehicles transporting dangerous substances will avoid the use of roads in densely populated areas and will not
They will travel through tunnels whose length is greater than 500 m, when they have a safe alternative route. The
The itinerary must be programmed in such a way as to avoid the presence of the vehicle transporting dangerous substances.
on roads with high traffic flow, during times of greatest traffic intensity (article 17).
Vehicles used to transport dangerous loads may only be parked for rest or
drivers' accommodation, in areas previously determined by the competent authority and, if there is no
such areas, parking in residential areas, public places or places with easy access to the public will be avoided.
(article 19).
- The verification of said regulations will be carried out through a checklist.

According to the Baseline of the project, archaeological finds were found in the area of influence
of the project. From the inspection carried out, only one archaeological site was recognized, called
PMP-SA-01, corresponding to a concentration of ceramic fragments from smoothed surfaces (interior and
exterior) of 146 m2, of possible historical temporality of indigenous tradition (judging by the presence of
fragments of smoothed surfaces, without lathe marks and with the use of antiplastics of the aggregate type
fine granulometry, although clearly visible), located inside the Maite ZE, in the area of a road
existing, whose coordinates are presented below.

In the event of an unforeseen paleontological discovery, the Owner will take into account what is indicated in Article 26 of the Law.
N°17,288 of National Monuments, proceeding as follows:
a) The works will stop at the place of discovery, at least 2 meters away around the point where the
produced, and if the discovery is multiple, 2 meters from the specimens furthest from the center should be considered.
of the place.
b) Notice will be given immediately to the construction manager or superior in charge of the work in the area of the discovery, and
will inform the Sustainability Area of the Owner company of its exact location.
c) The area will be correctly delimited and marked (signage, flag, etc.) for its protection.
In addition, there will be adequate signage indicating the restriction of entry to the sector, accompanied by
a perimeter fence that limits and protects the discovery.
d) The National Monuments Council (CMN) will be notified about the unforeseen discovery, using
UTM coordinates (DATUM WGS 84) and good resolution photographic record (with close-up shots,
detail, with scale and context in general). The notification will be made to the CMN by the person in charge of Media
Ambiente, or another representative of the owner, within a maximum period of five business days from the date of
discovery of the find.
On the other hand, for the archaeological component the following is considered:
If heritage elements are found, the works will stop at a distance of 2 m from the discovery.
marking and protecting evidence. Likewise, the discovery will be reported to the authority in response to the
current legislation. With respect to the archaeological component, based on heritage sensitivity to
The area welcomes permanent archaeological monitoring and heritage induction talks.
during the construction phase of the project. Likewise, this activity will be reported to
the SMA in a

14.10 Description of voluntary environmental commitments
14.10.1 Water Resources Commitment
CAV-01: Monitoring associated with flow control in the Penco estuary Reference EIA
Associated Impact Does not apply Chapter 13,
Project Phase to Section 13.2.1
Construction, operation and closure phase
which applies Table 13-3
Objective:
Monitor channel fluviometry (gauging) to establish or rule out impact on the water component
superficial.
Description:
Objective, The owner proposes the fluviometric control of the Penco estuary, through flow measurement stations (gauges), as it is
Description and a permanent channel close to the project environment.
Justification
Justification:
Monitoring corresponds to mechanisms normally used to establish or rule out effects on the
mentioned component. Without prejudice to the fact that the project does not consider the use of water from the Penco estuary, the owner
proposes to maintain the continuity of this monitoring throughout the useful life of the project.
14-266
==================================================================================
PAGE 271
==================================================================================
Chapter 14
Summary Tabs
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
CAV-01: Monitoring associated with flow control in the Penco estuary Reference EIA
The owner's proposal is to maintain flow records in this channel that has a permanent flow, where there will be no
works, on which in situ monitoring has been carried out for more than two years with which it has been possible to validate
their seasonal behavior, leaving this information available for those who want to access this information.
Location:
The following table indicates the points where gauging will be carried out in the Penco estuary.
Location of capacity points in Penco estuary
UTM COORDINATES 18 H. DATUM WGS-84
MONITORING POINT
EAST (m) NORTH (m)
P1 681,087 5,931,458
P2 681,408 5,931,666
Shape:
Measurement will be used by measuring with a windlass, a device made up of vanes that rotate when in contact with
a current of water, the number of revolutions being proportional to the speed of the current. It must be made present
Place, Form and that there is other equipment for carrying out flow measurements that will be evaluated according to the conditions
Opportunity of the measurement point or the implementation of new technologies. Without prejudice to the above, the considerations for this
Implementation activity are:
- The section must be chosen in an accessible place, according to the terrain conditions.
- The gauging must be carried out in a straight section of the watercourse, in a section without waterfalls, rapids or
turbulence.
- Capacity will be carried out by wading. This considers the location of a properly graduated tape along
width of the section of the channel, in which abscissa must be marked every 10 cm from left to right (in favor of the
flow), in which measurements of depth and speed of the water current must be made.
- The reel has a graduated bar, which must be placed vertically until it touches the bottom of the bed.
to record that depth and at that same point record the speed (number of turns of the reel) that
corresponds to the speed of water flow in that vertical.

CAV-05 Germplasm Conservation of Gomortega keule, Citronella mucronata and Pitavia punctata EIA Reference
Objective:
Expand the extent of the presence of the species Gomortega keule (queule), Citronella mucronata (naranjillo) and Pitavia
punctata (pitao), as well as its area of occupation, with a view to improving the indicators of the International Union for the
Conservation of Nature (IUCN) that define the current conservation status of the species.
Description:
The commitment considers the rescue of genetic material to carry out an ex situ conservation plan, maintaining
part of the local populations of Gomortega keule, Citronella mucronata and Pitavia punctata outside the area of origin.
As a criterion of additionality and faced with a climate change scenario, it is proposed to build a garden of
Objective, varieties in a locality located further south, outside the area of current occupation of the three species, with minors
description and water restrictions, but with thermal stability due to proximity to bodies of water. The variety garden corresponds to
justification an ex situ conservation practice, where the adaptation of populations of Gomortega keule, Citronella will be evaluated
mucronata and Pitavia punctata and the necessary cultural care will be carried out to have a representative replica
of the genetic variability of the population
local ion where the Project will be located.
Justification:
The proposed measure aims to contribute to the increase of CCP individuals in the committed sector by maintaining
the genetic base of their populations, for this it contemplates the collection of the germplasm of origin for the propagation to
from individuals present in the area of influence of the Project.
Sexual and asexual propagation will be implemented in order to obtain an adequate number of plants for the programs
enrichment and research in situ. Additionally, the owner proposes an ex situ conservation bank, in order to
expand the presence of these species to other locations.
Location:
The rescue of germplasm (fruits/seeds and cuttings), of the species in the queule, naranjillo and pitao category, will be carried out
Place, form and
from selected individuals in areas of native preservation forest, or in surrounding areas in the area of
opportunity to
influence of the Project, without affecting the survival or reproductive capacity of the individuals in obtaining the material
implementation
of propagation.

For the production of plants, a strategic union with local nurseries is considered, considering the supervision and
technical advice, in addition to the construction of its own infrastructure for the reception and conditioning of these, the
which will be located in the area of influence of the project.
Shape:
The reproductive material (fruits/seeds and cuttings) of the individuals of queule, naranjillo and
pitao among other species and the appropriate production protocols will be applied for each species
considering the technological particularities of each nursery involved.
Once the plants are developed and meet the desirable quality guidelines, they will be transferred to the area of influence of the
project to an infrastructure that allows its conditioning and transfer to the revegetation sites.
On the other hand, the actions for the implementation of a variety garden in the town of Frutillar, in
the Los Lagos Region. The garden is initially planned to be installed and maintained at the Experimental Station.
Frutillar from the University of Chile. The above will allow the care and monitoring of the specimens in an environment
more humid. The variety garden will have provenances of the Gomortega species. keule, Citronella mucronata and
Pitavia punctata. This type of ex situ conservation aims to ensure the continuity of the species beyond its limits.
current natural distribution. The idea is to expand the extent of the species' presence, as well as its area of
occupation, with a view to removing the species from their current IUCN status.
As an alternative instance, other locations may be explored that ensure the permanence of the material and its dissemination.
of the results obtained. In this way, the Project will be able to evaluate the installation and care of this commitment, in
another place in the Lakes Region with similar edaphoclimatic conditions to those of the experimental station of the
Frutillar commune.
In the propagation efforts, tests are proposed where the different techniques registered for the
propagation of the species, as long as the most appropriate treatment is available for plant production.

articles 26 and 27 of Law 17,288 on National Monuments and articles 20 and 23 of the Regulation on

Description:

approved by the CMN and that will be dictated by this or another qualified professional (with verifiable experience in
Paleontology) under the supervision of the paleontologist in charge. These talks will be aimed at workers and the respective
headquarters, in which the basic concepts and notions about the paleontological heritage associated with the
Project. Contents such as:
- Paleontological context of the area, the possible findings that could be presented and how to identify them.
- The regulatory framework that protects paleont materials
logic and the action protocol in the event of a possible finding
paleontological.
The talks will be held prior to the start of the works and for each new worker who is incorporated into the Project.
once its construction has begun.
The talks will inform workers about the paleontological context of the area, the possible findings that could
present themselves and how to identify them, the regulatory framework that protects paleontological materials and the action protocol
before a possible discovery.
The reports of these activities will be sent to the authority (SMA and CMN) by the Paleontologist in charge, periodically.
monthly, including the following items:
a. Name and signature of the professional who conducted the induction talk.
b. Contents of the induction carried out.
c. Copy of the graphic material presented to the attendees.
d. Photographic and/or audiovisual record of the activity.
and. Synthesis of comments, observations and questions made by the attendees.
