CAV-10: Action protocol for paleontological findings EIA Reference
Associated impact Possible impact
ion of paleontological materials and geological units that could contain them Chapter 13,
Section 13.2.4
Project phase Construction and operation
Table 13-12
to which it applies
Objective:
Provide the paleontologist and the workers who will participate in the construction phase of the Project, a mechanism of
standard action to follow in the event of a possible paleontological discovery situation, ensuring the safeguarding and protection of the
paleontological materials found.
Description:
If an activity or work, whether manual or with machinery, faces a situation of possible discovery of fossils, be they
those expected due to bibliographical or unexpected antecedents, the following procedure must be followed, based on what
generically recommended by the National Monuments Council:
objective,
1. Whether the discovery is made by the paleontologist monitor or by a construction worker, the discovery must be stopped.
description and
activity or work in that sector. If the finding is detected by a worker in the absence of the paleontologist monitor,
justification
The worker must immediately notify the superior in charge of the work in the area of the discovery and this
The paleontologist in charge will be immediately notified to come to the site of the discovery. The
activities at the site of the discovery nor will construction personnel pass through. The boss must also be informed of the discovery.
of work and the Department of the Environment, or similar, that represents the owner of the Project.
2. The paleontologist monitor will have to assess a priori whether it may be an isolated find or a site
paleontological (bed or stratum with fossils) and delimit it to segregate and protect the area around the discovery.
To do this, the paleontologist must carry out a detailed visual inspection, taking into account that it cannot be carried out
any type of excavation, intervention or clearing of the area or findings. If it is estimated that the finding
corresponds to an isolated material, the area must be segregated 2 meters away around the place of discovery,
14-289
==================================================================================
PAGE 294
==================================================================================
Chapter 14
Summary Tabs
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
CAV-10: Action protocol for paleontological findings EIA Reference
while, if the discovery corresponds to a site of multiple specimens or fragments, 2 will be considered
meters away from the materials furthest from the center of the place.
3. The area must be correctly delimited and marked for its protection, in the first instance with flags or
cones and adequate signage indicating the restriction of entry to the sector. Within this segregated area there is no
will carry out work or transit of personnel, and only the Paleontologist in charge and his/her staff may enter it.
collaborators. After the inspection by the Paleontologist, a fence must be implemented
perimeter (2 meters high) that limits and protects the final segregated area, along with the aforementioned signage.
4. Sectoral permission will be requested from the National Monuments Council to be able to collect the assets.
paleontological, with or without excavation. In this request, the background information about the discovery will be provided.
paleontological using UTM coordinates (DATUM WGS 84) and good resolution photographic record (with
in close-up, detail, scale and context in general). The request must be made by a professional
paleontologist whose curricular information is in accordance with CMN Res. Ex. No. 650 of 2022. Along with the application
and the information of the find, a methodology integrated with the ongoing paleontological monitoring will be proposed for the
recovery of the discovery made and future findings of similar characteristics or, on the other hand, a methodology
of particular excavation for the discovery.
In the case of a complex discovery and/or paleontological site, along with the permit application
and the information of the find, a collection and/or paleontological excavation methodology will be proposed for this
type of findings. If necessary, the proposal will include a professional with training and/or experience in
paleontological excavations to be in charge of it.
If you are neither the monitor nor the owner of the
permission, you must be in coordination with these people to make decisions during the excavation
paleontological.
5. Whether part or all of the discovery, whether normal, complex or paleontological site (bed or stratum), is
located outside the area of influence of the project, in the application for the sectoral permit the
this circumstance, including in the background the justification of the need to intervene in a limited area
outside the area of influence of the Project.
6. With all the above, the CMN will grant the permit and determine the measures to implement, considering the Law
N°17,288 of National Monuments and the Excavation Regulations D.S. No. 484 of 1990. The owner of the Project
must assume all the expenses generated by these measures, including the hiring of competent personnel to
carry them out, including collecting and packaging the rescued fossils (if applicable).

project to the
what applies
Objective:
Establish the participation of the communities in the area of influence of the Project, keeping them informed about the
various activities and works that will be carried out during the useful life of the project, strengthening collaboration and trust
between the owner and the local community.
The main purpose is to inform about the protection of those environmental elements that are relevant to the
Community and that can be related to the project works.
Description:
Disseminate information regarding works and activities, implementing permanent and open communication,
objective,
description and using, for this purpose, expeditious communication channels and specific response deadlines. Through them,
justification will inform the activities and address possible problems that the Project works could generate. The information
that will be delivered to the community will contain execution dates and implementation measures. In addition to this, it will include
information sign in the project site area.
Justification:
The delivery of timely information about the Project's works and milestones will allow people to organize their
activities against possible effects on the works and activities of the Project, so as not to generate uncertainty
with them and minimize the effects on the usual practices of people in the sectors close to the project.
Location:
The commitment will be implemented in the area of influence of the Project.
Place, form and
Implementation form opportunity:
implementation
Prior to each of the phases of the project, the Owner will arrange a monitoring team to deliver information
environmental of the project and its measures in order to physically ensure the delivery of information and strengthen the link
with the community. For this, the monitoring program and activities in the communities will be articulated in a timely manner with the community.
